The Proof of God's Eternity from Necessary Existence
Razi states the proof of God's eternity from necessary existence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how the attribute of necessary existence directly implies God's eternity, and why no separate argument is needed.

Core Idea
Necessary existence cannot cease; therefore, God is eternal without beginning or end.

In this passage, Imam Razi presents a concise yet profound argument: once we accept that God exists necessarily by Himself, His eternity follows logically. The necessity of His existence means He cannot be subject to non-existence, which demands that He has always existed and will always exist. Let's see how Razi establishes this connection.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Familiarize yourself with Razi's statement and its literal meaning. Notice the logical flow from necessary existence to eternity.
Pay attention to the key terms: qadim, azali, abadi, sarmadi.
2
Identify the logical chain
Razi argues: Necessary existent -> cannot accept non-existence -> must be eternal. Trace each step.
This chain is the core proof.
3
Compare with earlier theologians
Razi mentions that earlier theologians used other methods. Reflect on why his method is more direct.
He still presents their views later as a blessing.
4
Reflect on the implication
Why does necessary existence necessarily entail eternity? Because if something is necessary, it cannot be preceded by non-existence or followed by non-existence.
This is a key insight of Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة الرابعة في أن الله تعالى قديم أزلي أبدي سرمدي جميع اعلم أنا لما دللنا في المسألة الثالثة على وجوب انتهاء الممكنات إلى موجود واجب الوجود لذاته وكل ما كان واجب الوجود لذاته فإن حقيقته لا تقبل العدم أصلا، وكل ما كان كذلك فإنه يجب أن يكون قديما أزليا باقيا أبديًا، فعلى هذا لا نحتاج بعد ذلك إلى إقامة الدلالة على كونه تعالى أبديًا إلا أن المتكلمين الذين كانوا قبلنا لما لم يذكروا تلك الطريقة في إثبات واجب الوجود لا جرم كانوا معولين في إثبات كونه تعالى أزليّا أبديًا على وجوه أخر، فنحن أردنا أن نتبرك بإيراد تلك الوجوه أيضا.
The Fourth Question: On that God Most High is eternal, everlasting, perpetual, all. Know that when we proved in the Third Question the necessity of contingent things ending at an existent that is necessary in itself, and everything that is necessary in itself, its reality in no way accepts non-existence, and everything that is such, it must be eternal, pre-eternal, remaining forever, so accordingly we do not need after that to establish a proof for His being everlasting, except that the theologians who were before us, since they did not mention that method in proving the Necessary Existent, inevitably they relied in proving His being pre-eternal and everlasting on other aspects, so we wanted to seek blessing by presenting those aspects as well.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage is a definition of the doctrine of God's eternity and a proof. Razi begins by stating the topic: that God is eternal, everlasting, and perpetual. He then explains that the proof of God's necessary existence (established in the previous question) directly implies that He is eternal (azali) and everlasting (abadi/sarmadi). Because the necessary existent cannot accept non-existence, so it must be without beginning and without end. Therefore, no separate argument for eternity is needed. However, earlier theologians did not use this method of proving the Necessary Existent, so they relied on other arguments. Razi says he will present those other arguments as a blessing.

Key Terms
قديم (qadim)
أزلي (azali)
أبدي (abadi)
سرمدي (sarmadi)
واجب الوجود (wajib al-wujud)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that proving God's necessary existence is a separate proof from His eternity, but Razi shows they are directly linked.
Correction: Razi argues that necessary existence directly entails eternity because what is necessary cannot be preceded or followed by non-existence.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, why is no separate proof needed for God's eternity after proving His necessary existence?
A) Because the necessary existence implies impossibility of non-existence, which demands eternity.
B) Because the world is eternal, so God must be eternal.
C) Because earlier theologians already proved it.
D) Because the Quran explicitly states it.

Key Takeaway
God's necessary existence directly implies His eternity; no separate proof is needed.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence is necessary and cannot cease, while your existence is contingent and could be annihilated at any moment, how should that reshape your daily priorities and reliance on Him?
?
Razi says the necessary existent's reality does not accept non-existence. Have you ever truly internalized that God alone is self-sufficient and everything else depends on Him? What would change in your life if you lived with constant awareness of that fact?
?
The passage links necessary existence directly to eternity. If God is eternal, then He has always been and always will be—while you exist only for a fleeting moment. Does that perspective make you feel insignificant, or liberated from the illusion of self-sufficiency? How will you respond?

The Theologians' Proof and the First Objection
Razi states the proof and the first objection from intermediaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the theologians' proof of God's eternity and the first objection that posits a chain of intermediaries, and why this objection must be refuted.

Core Idea
An infinite regress is impossible, but can a chain of originated beings end in an eternal maker?

Razi opens by restating the classic kalam proof: the world needs a Maker, and if that Maker were originated, it would need another, leading to an impossible infinite regress. Therefore, the Maker must be eternal. But an objection arises: why not allow a finite chain of originated beings that ultimately terminates in an eternal being, as the Mufawwida and philosophers claim? Razi acknowledges this possibility and insists it must be refuted, setting the stage for his detailed response.

Guided Path
1
Read the proof for God's eternity
Read the opening sentences where Razi states the theologians' argument: the world needs a Maker, and infinite regress (tasalsul) is impossible, so the Maker is eternal (qadim).
Notice the logical structure: if B, then infinite regress, which is impossible, so not B.
2
Understand the first objection
The objection says: why can't the creator of this world be originated, while its creator is eternal? This avoids infinite regress. Razi mentions that the Mufawwida and philosophers hold such views.
The Mufawwida delegate creation to planets; philosophers posit active intellects.
3
See why it must be refuted
Razi says this possibility exists and therefore must be refuted. This shows the importance of addressing alternative explanations.
The refutation will come later in the text.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مشايخ المتكلمين لما أقاموا الدلالة على افتقار العالم إلى صانع قالوا: صانع العالم لو كان محدثًا لافتقر إلى محدث آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وهو محال، فوجب القول بأن صانع العالم قديم. فإن قيل : الإشكال على هذا الاستدلال من وجوه : الأول: لِمَ لا يجوز أن يقال : خالق هذا العالم المحسوس شيء محدث، وخالق ذلك المحدث شيء قديم، وعلى هذا التقدير يكون صانع العالم محدثًا ولا يلزم التسلسل أيضاً، وهذا هو قول المفوضة وأصحاب الوسائط، ألا ترى أن الفلاسفة يقولون : مدبر ما تحت كرة القمر هو العقل، وهذا العقل الفعال معلول عقل آخر، وذلك العقل معلول عقل آخر إلى عشر مراتب وأكثر، ثم ذلك العقل الأول معلول وجود الله تعالى، وعند المفوضة: الإله الأكبر خلق السيارات السبع، وفوض تدبير هذا العالم إليها، وإذا كان هذا الاحتمال قائمًا فلا بد من إبطاله. السؤال الثاني: أن كل موجودين يُفْرَضَان فلا بد وأن يكونا إما معا أو يكون أحدهما سابقًا على الآخر، فإن كانا معًا لزم أن يكونا قديمين أو محدثين، لكنكم تقولون : الإله قديم والعالم محدث، وإن كان أحدهما قبل الآخر فتقدم أحدهما على الآخر إما أن يكون بمقدار متناه أو غير متناه، فإن كان بمقدار متناه كان كل واحد منهما محدثاً، وذلك محال، وإن كان بمقدار غير متناه فذلك محال لوجوه. الأول : أنه على هذا التقدير قد يكون انقضاء قبل اليوم مدة غير متناهية، وانقضاء ما لا نهاية له غير معقول. الثاني : أنه إن كان يتوقف حصول اليوم على أن يقضي قبله ما لا نهاية - وانقضاء غير المتناهي محال، والموقوف على المحال محال ـ فوجب أن يمتنع حصول اليوم، وحيث حصل اليوم علمنا أن المنقضي متناه لا غير متناه. الثالث: أن المنقضي من زمان الطوفان إلى الأزل أقل من المنقضي من زماننا هذا إلى الأزل، فإذا طبقنا بين هاتين الجملتين من هذين الطرفين اللذين يلياننا وجب أن يظهر التفاوت من طرف الأزل وإلا لكان البعض مثل الكل، فتكون المدة المنقضية متناهية، فيكون تقدم الله تعالى على العالم متناهيا. الرابع : أنه لما كان تقدم الله على العالم أمرًا واجب الثبوت، وهذا التقدم لا يتقرر إلا بهذه المدة كان دوام ذات الله تعالى واستمرار بقائه مفتقرًا إلى تحقيق هذه المدة، والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن لذاته، فيلزم أن يكون واجب الوجود لذاته ممكن الوجود لذاته، وهذا خلف. الخامس : أن المدة لا تُعقل إلا بتعاقب الآنات وتوالي الأزمنة والساعات، فلو كان الباري تعالى متقدمًا على العالم بمدة لا نهاية لها ولا أول لها لزم حصول الأزمنة المتوالية في الأزل، وذلك محال ؛ لأن توالي بعض الأزمنة بالبعض يقتضي كون كل واحد منها مسبوقاً بغيره، والأزل عبارة عن نفي المسبوقية بالغير، والجمع بينهما متناقض. ولا يقال : هذه الإشكالات إنما تلزم إذا قلنا : إن الله تعالى قبل العالم وسابق عليه بمدة موجودة وزمان متحقق ونحن لا نقول بذلك، بل نقول: إنه تعالى سابق على العالم بمدة مفروضة موهومة لا تحقق لها خارج الذهن لأنا نقول: هذا الكلام ضعيف جداً، لأن تقدم الباري تعالى على العالم إذا كان حاصلا لا بحسب فرضنا واعتبارنا بل بحسب الحقيقة والوجود سواء وجد الفرض أو لم يوجد، ثم ثبت أن هذا التقدم والسبق ليس إلا بمدة متناهية وجب أن يكون حصول تلك المدة لا بحسب الفرض فقط، بل بحسب الوجود والتحقق.
And know that when the masters of the theologians established the proof of the world's need for a Maker, they said: The Maker of the world, if He were originated, would need another originator, and there would follow an infinite regress, which is impossible. So it is necessary to say that the Maker of the world is eternal. If it is said: The objection to this argument is from several aspects: First: Why is it not permitted to say that the creator of this sensible world is an originated thing, and the creator of that originated thing is an eternal thing, and on this estimation the Maker of the world would be originated and infinite regress would not follow either? This is the statement of the Mufawwida and the proponents of intermediaries. Do you not see that the philosophers say: The manager of what is under the sphere of the moon is the intellect, and this active intellect is an effect of another intellect, and that intellect is an effect of another intellect up to ten levels or more, then that first intellect is an effect of the existence of God Most High. And according to the Mufawwida: The greatest deity created the seven planets and delegated the management of this world to them. And when this possibility exists, it must be refuted. The second question: That any two existents that are supposed, they must either be together or one of them be prior to the other. If they are together, it follows that they are both eternal or both originated. But you say: God is eternal and the world is originated. And if one is prior to the other, then the priority of one over the other is either by a finite amount or an infinite amount. If it is by a finite amount, then each of them is originated, and that is impossible. And if it is by an infinite amount, that is impossible for several reasons: First: That on this estimation, there would have passed before today an infinite duration, and the passing of what has no end is unintelligible. Second: That if the occurrence of today depends on the passing before it of what is infinite — and the passing of the infinite is impossible, and what depends on the impossible is impossible — then it must be that the occurrence of today is impossible, and since today has occurred, we know that what has passed is finite, not infinite. Third: That what has passed from the time of the Flood to eternity is less than what has passed from our time to eternity. So if we compare these two sums from these two ends that are adjacent to us, the disparity must appear from the side of eternity, otherwise the part would be like the whole, so the duration that has passed would be finite, and thus God's priority over the world would be finite. Fourth: That since God's priority over the world is a necessarily established matter, and this priority is not realized except through this duration, then the duration of God's essence and the continuity of His persistence would depend on the actualization of this duration. And what depends on another is possible in itself, so it would follow that the Necessary Existent in itself is possible in itself, which is a contradiction. Fifth: That duration is not intelligible except through the succession of moments and the sequence of times and hours. So if the Creator was prior to the world by a duration that has no end and no beginning, it would necessitate the occurrence of successive times in eternity, which is impossible, because the sequence of some times after others necessitates that each of them is preceded by another, and eternity is the expression of the negation of precedence by another, and combining them is contradictory. And it is not said: These difficulties only arise if we say that God Most High is before the world and prior to it by an existing duration and a realized time, and we do not say that. Rather, we say: He is prior to the world by a supposed, imagined duration that has no realization outside the mind. [But] we say: This statement is very weak, because if the priority of the Creator over the world is actual, not according to our supposition and consideration, but according to reality and existence, whether the supposition exists or not, and then it is established that this priority and precedence is only by a finite duration, then it must be that the occurrence of that duration is not only according to supposition, but according to existence and realization.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage contains two objections to the theologians' proof of God's eternity and their refutation. Razi begins by stating the proof: the world needs a Maker; if the Maker were originated, it would need another originator, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible, so the Maker must be eternal (qadim). Then the first objection: why not accept a chain of intermediaries ending in an eternal being? This is the view of the Mufawwida (those who delegate) and the philosophers who posit active intellects. Razi notes that this possibility must be refuted. The second objection is more elaborate: given two existents, either they are together (both eternal or both originated) or one precedes the other. If the precedence is finite, both are originated; if infinite, it is impossible for five reasons. Razi lists these five reasons: 1) an infinite past would have to elapse before today, which is unintelligible (ghayr ma'qul); 2) if today depends on an infinite past, which is impossible, then today is impossible, but it exists, so the past must be finite; 3) the time from the Flood to eternity is less than from now to eternity, so by comparison the past must be finite; 4) if God's priority requires an infinite duration, then His persistence depends on that duration, making the Necessary Existent (wajib al-wujud) contingent (mumkin), a contradiction; 5) infinite successive times in eternity (azal) is contradictory because eternity negates precedence (sabq), but successive times require each to be preceded by another. Finally, Razi addresses a counter-argument that these difficulties only arise if we consider the priority as a real time, while we say it is only a mental supposition. Razi refutes this: the priority is real, not merely mental, and it has been proven that the duration is finite, so it must be real.

Key Terms
تسلسل (tasalsul)
مفوضة (Mufawwida)
وسائط (wasait)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that an infinite regress can be avoided by having an originated being created by an eternal being directly, but the objection claims a chain of originated beings ending in an eternal being is also possible.
Correction: Razi shows that this objection must be refuted because it challenges the proof. The refutation will demonstrate why such a chain is impossible or unnecessary.

Checkpoint
According to Razi, what is the first objection to the theologians' proof?
A) The world does not need a Maker.
B) The Maker could be originated but created by an eternal being, avoiding infinite regress.
C) The world is eternal and needs no Maker.
D) The proof relies on an invalid assumption.

Key Takeaway
The theologians' proof of God's eternity is challenged by the possibility of a chain of intermediaries, which Razi must refute.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objection suggests God could delegate the world's management to intermediaries. In your own life, do you sometimes rely on secondary causes—people, circumstances, your own efforts—as if they were independent from God? How does this lesson's insistence on refuting such delegation challenge you to turn directly to the Eternal Maker in your needs?
?
If the theologians' proof is true that the Maker must be eternal, then everything else is originated and dependent. When you face a situation where you feel helpless, do you instinctively seek help from the Eternal or from temporary things? What would it look like for you to live today with the conviction that only the Eternal is truly sufficient?

The Second Objection: Finite vs. Infinite Priority
Razi presents the second objection with five arguments against infinite priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the second objection to the proof of God's eternity — that if God is prior to the world, the priority must be either finite or infinite, and both lead to contradictions — and will grasp the five reasons why infinite priority is impossible.

Core Idea
If God is prior to the world, the priority must be finite, but that would make God originated; infinite priority is impossible for five reasons.

The second objection is more elaborate: given any two existents, they are either simultaneous (both eternal or both originated) or one precedes the other. If the precedence is finite, both are originated; if infinite, it leads to absurdities. Razi then presents five detailed arguments showing why an infinite past duration before the world is impossible, thus forcing the conclusion that the world must be eternal alongside God — unless the proof can be salvaged. But Razi is presenting these as objections to be refuted later.

Guided Path
1
Understand the dilemma of two existents
Razi sets up a dichotomy: any two existents are either together or one precedes the other. If together, both are either eternal or originated. If one precedes, the priority is either finite or infinite.
This is a logical partition of possibilities.
2
Identify the five reasons against infinite priority
Read each of the five reasons carefully. They are labeled with ordinal numbers in the Arabic text (الأول, الثاني, etc.).
These reasons are arguments that an infinite past is impossible.
3
Take note of the structure of each reason
Each reason is a self-contained argument. For example, the first says that an infinite duration cannot have 'passed' because it has no end. The second uses the dependence of today on an infinite past to show today would be impossible.
These are classic arguments against the eternity of the world (qidam al-alam).
4
See how these refute the possibility of infinite priority
If infinite priority is impossible, and finite priority would make God originated, then the only remaining possibility is that God and the world are simultaneous — but that would make both eternal or both originated. The theologians want God eternal and world originated, so this objection is a challenge.
Razi is presenting the objection; he will later refute it (perhaps in the next lesson).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن مشايخ المتكلمين لما أقاموا الدلالة على افتقار العالم إلى صانع قالوا: صانع العالم لو كان محدثًا لافتقر إلى محدث آخر، ولزم التسلسل، وهو محال، فوجب القول بأن صانع العالم قديم. فإن قيل : الإشكال على هذا الاستدلال من وجوه : الأول: لِمَ لا يجوز أن يقال : خالق هذا العالم المحسوس شيء محدث، وخالق ذلك المحدث شيء قديم، وعلى هذا التقدير يكون صانع العالم محدثًا ولا يلزم التسلسل أيضاً، وهذا هو قول المفوضة وأصحاب الوسائط، ألا ترى أن الفلاسفة يقولون : مدبر ما تحت كرة القمر هو العقل، وهذا العقل الفعال معلول عقل آخر، وذلك العقل معلول عقل آخر إلى عشر مراتب وأكثر، ثم ذلك العقل الأول معلول وجود الله تعالى، وعند المفوضة: الإله الأكبر خلق السيارات السبع، وفوض تدبير هذا العالم إليها، وإذا كان هذا الاحتمال قائمًا فلا بد من إبطاله. السؤال الثاني: أن كل موجودين يُفْرَضَان فلا بد وأن يكونا إما معا أو يكون أحدهما سابقًا على الآخر، فإن كانا معًا لزم أن يكونا قديمين أو محدثين، لكنكم تقولون : الإله قديم والعالم محدث، وإن كان أحدهما قبل الآخر فتقدم أحدهما على الآخر إما أن يكون بمقدار متناه أو غير متناه، فإن كان بمقدار متناه كان كل واحد منهما محدثاً، وذلك محال، وإن كان بمقدار غير متناه فذلك محال لوجوه. الأول : أنه على هذا التقدير قد يكون انقضاء قبل اليوم مدة غير متناهية، وانقضاء ما لا نهاية له غير معقول. الثاني : أنه إن كان يتوقف حصول اليوم على أن يقضي قبله ما لا نهاية - وانقضاء غير المتناهي محال، والموقوف على المحال محال ـ فوجب أن يمتنع حصول اليوم، وحيث حصل اليوم علمنا أن المنقضي متناه لا غير متناه. الثالث: أن المنقضي من زمان الطوفان إلى الأزل أقل من المنقضي من زماننا هذا إلى الأزل، فإذا طبقنا بين هاتين الجملتين من هذين الطرفين اللذين يلياننا وجب أن يظهر التفاوت من طرف الأزل وإلا لكان البعض مثل الكل، فتكون المدة المنقضية متناهية، فيكون تقدم الله تعالى على العالم متناهيا. الرابع : أنه لما كان تقدم الله على العالم أمرًا واجب الثبوت، وهذا التقدم لا يتقرر إلا بهذه المدة كان دوام ذات الله تعالى واستمرار بقائه مفتقرًا إلى تحقيق هذه المدة، والمفتقر إلى الغير ممكن لذاته، فيلزم أن يكون واجب الوجود لذاته ممكن الوجود لذاته، وهذا خلف. الخامس : أن المدة لا تُعقل إلا بتعاقب الآنات وتوالي الأزمنة والساعات، فلو كان الباري تعالى متقدمًا على العالم بمدة لا نهاية لها ولا أول لها لزم حصول الأزمنة المتوالية في الأزل، وذلك محال ؛ لأن توالي بعض الأزمنة بالبعض يقتضي كون كل واحد منها مسبوقاً بغيره، والأزل عبارة عن نفي المسبوقية بالغير، والجمع بينهما متناقض. ولا يقال : هذه الإشكالات إنما تلزم إذا قلنا : إن الله تعالى قبل العالم وسابق عليه بمدة موجودة وزمان متحقق ونحن لا نقول بذلك، بل نقول: إنه تعالى سابق على العالم بمدة مفروضة موهومة لا تحقق لها خارج الذهن لأنا نقول: هذا الكلام ضعيف جداً، لأن تقدم الباري تعالى على العالم إذا كان حاصلا لا بحسب فرضنا واعتبارنا بل بحسب الحقيقة والوجود سواء وجد الفرض أو لم يوجد، ثم ثبت أن هذا التقدم والسبق ليس إلا بمدة متناهية وجب أن يكون حصول تلك المدة لا بحسب الفرض فقط، بل بحسب الوجود والتحقق.
And know that when the masters of the theologians established the proof of the world's need for a Maker, they said: The Maker of the world, if He were originated, would need another originator, and there would follow an infinite regress, which is impossible. So it is necessary to say that the Maker of the world is eternal. If it is said: The objection to this argument is from several aspects: First: Why is it not permitted to say that the creator of this sensible world is an originated thing, and the creator of that originated thing is an eternal thing, and on this estimation the Maker of the world would be originated and infinite regress would not follow either? This is the statement of the Mufawwida and the proponents of intermediaries. Do you not see that the philosophers say: The manager of what is under the sphere of the moon is the intellect, and this active intellect is an effect of another intellect, and that intellect is an effect of another intellect up to ten levels or more, then that first intellect is an effect of the existence of God Most High. And according to the Mufawwida: The greatest deity created the seven planets and delegated the management of this world to them. And when this possibility exists, it must be refuted. The second question: That any two existents that are supposed, they must either be together or one of them be prior to the other. If they are together, it follows that they are both eternal or both originated. But you say: God is eternal and the world is originated. And if one is prior to the other, then the priority of one over the other is either by a finite amount or an infinite amount. If it is by a finite amount, then each of them is originated, and that is impossible. And if it is by an infinite amount, that is impossible for several reasons: First: That on this estimation, there would have passed before today an infinite duration, and the passing of what has no end is unintelligible. Second: That if the occurrence of today depends on the passing before it of what is infinite — and the passing of the infinite is impossible, and what depends on the impossible is impossible — then it must be that the occurrence of today is impossible, and since today has occurred, we know that what has passed is finite, not infinite. Third: That what has passed from the time of the Flood to eternity is less than what has passed from our time to eternity. So if we compare these two sums from these two ends that are adjacent to us, the disparity must appear from the side of eternity, otherwise the part would be like the whole, so the duration that has passed would be finite, and thus God's priority over the world would be finite. Fourth: That since God's priority over the world is a necessarily established matter, and this priority is not realized except through this duration, then the duration of God's essence and the continuity of His persistence would depend on the actualization of this duration. And what depends on another is possible in itself, so it would follow that the Necessary Existent in itself is possible in itself, which is a contradiction. Fifth: That duration is not intelligible except through the succession of moments and the sequence of times and hours. So if the Creator was prior to the world by a duration that has no end and no beginning, it would necessitate the occurrence of successive times in eternity, which is impossible, because the sequence of some times after others necessitates that each of them is preceded by another, and eternity is the expression of the negation of precedence by another, and combining them is contradictory. And it is not said: These difficulties only arise if we say that God Most High is before the world and prior to it by an existing duration and a realized time, and we do not say that. Rather, we say: He is prior to the world by a supposed, imagined duration that has no realization outside the mind. [But] we say: This statement is very weak, because if the priority of the Creator over the world is actual, not according to our supposition and consideration, but according to reality and existence, whether the supposition exists or not, and then it is established that this priority and precedence is only by a finite duration, then it must be that the occurrence of that duration is not only according to supposition, but according to existence and realization.
Source pages p. 93

Commentary
This passage contains two objections to the theologians' proof of God's eternity and their refutation. Razi begins by stating the proof: the world needs a Maker; if the Maker were originated, it would need another originator, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible, so the Maker must be eternal (qadim). Then the first objection: why not accept a chain of intermediaries ending in an eternal being? This is the view of the Mufawwida (those who delegate) and the philosophers who posit active intellects. Razi notes that this possibility must be refuted. The second objection is more elaborate: given two existents, either they are together (both eternal or both originated) or one precedes the other. If the precedence is finite, both are originated; if infinite, it is impossible for five reasons. Razi lists these five reasons: 1) an infinite past would have to elapse before today, which is unintelligible (ghayr ma'qul); 2) if today depends on an infinite past, which is impossible, then today is impossible, but it exists, so the past must be finite; 3) the time from the Flood to eternity is less than from now to eternity, so by comparison the past must be finite; 4) if God's priority requires an infinite duration, then His persistence depends on that duration, making the Necessary Existent (wajib al-wujud) contingent (mumkin), a contradiction; 5) infinite successive times in eternity (azal) is contradictory because eternity negates precedence (sabq), but successive times require each to be preceded by another. Finally, Razi addresses a counter-argument that these difficulties only arise if we consider the priority as a real time, while we say it is only a mental supposition. Razi refutes this: the priority is real, not merely mental, and it has been proven that the duration is finite, so it must be real.

Key Terms
متناهٍ (mutanahi)
غير متناهٍ (ghayr mutanahi)
أزل (azal)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that if God is eternal and the world is originated, then there must be an infinite temporal gap between them, which is possible.
Correction: Razi shows that an infinite temporal gap leads to multiple logical absurdities, so the priority cannot be infinite; it must be finite, which would make God originated, contradicting His eternity.

Checkpoint
According to the second objection, if God's priority over the world is infinite, which of the following is a reason it is impossible?
A) The world would be eternal.
B) An infinite duration cannot have elapsed before today.
C) God would be originated.
D) The world would be created ex nihilo.

Key Takeaway
The second objection argues that any priority of God over the world must be either finite or infinite, but both lead to contradictions, thus challenging the proof of God's eternity.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
The objection argues that infinite priority leads to contradictions. When you think about God's existence before creation, do you ever feel a tension between your finite mind and the infinite reality? How do you reconcile that intellectually and spiritually?
?
If you were confronted with the claim that God's priority must be finite—making Him originated—what would your response be? Is your belief in God's eternity merely inherited, or have you truly grappled with these objections?
?
The proof of God's eternity relies on logical necessity. Has your faith in God's eternity ever been shaken by doubts? How would you defend it if challenged like the philosophers here, and does your certainty affect your daily worship?

Refuting the Mental Priority Counter-Argument
Razi refutes the counter-argument that God's priority is only mental.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the counter-argument that God's priority over the world is only mental (not real) and Razi's refutation that if the priority is real, the duration must be real and finite, thus the proof stands.

Core Idea
God's priority over the world is real, not merely mental, so the objections based on temporal priority cannot be dismissed as imaginary.

After presenting the second objection with its five reasons, Razi anticipates a possible escape: someone might say that these difficulties only arise if we consider God's priority as a real time, but we can say it is merely a mental supposition. Razi rejects this, arguing that the priority is real and has been proven to be finite by the earlier arguments, so the duration must be real as well. This refutes the attempt to sidestep the objection.

Guided Path
1
Read the counter-argument
The counter-argument states that the difficulties only apply if we consider God's priority as an actual existing time, but we can say it is only a mental concept.
This is a common move in kalam to avoid temporal implications.
2
Understand Razi's refutation
Razi argues that the priority is real, not just mental. It has been established that this priority is only by a finite duration, so that duration must also be real.
The refutation relies on the conclusion from the five reasons that the duration is finite.
3
Appreciate the strength of the refutation
Razi shows that even if the priority is real, it is finite, so the objections about infinite regress do not apply. The proof of God's eternity is thus not harmed.
This concludes the passage, but the full resolution of the objection may require further argument.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And know that when the masters of the theologians established the proof of the world's need for a Maker, they said: The Maker of the world, if He were originated, would need another originator, and there would follow an infinite regress, which is impossible. If they are together, it follows that they are both eternal or both originated. But you say: God is eternal and the world is originated. And if one is prior to the other, then the priority of one over the other is either by a finite amount or an infinite amount. If it is by a finite amount, then each of them is originated, and that is impossible. And if it is by an infinite amount, that is impossible for several reasons: First: That on this estimation, there would have passed before today an infinite duration, and the passing of what has no end is unintelligible. Commentary
This passage contains two objections to the theologians' proof of God's eternity and their refutation. Razi begins by stating the proof: the world needs a Maker; if the Maker were originated, it would need another originator, leading to an infinite regress (tasalsul), which is impossible, so the Maker must be eternal (qadim). Razi's Answers to Objections on God's Precedence
Razi answers two objections about God's priority.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how Razi defends the concept of God's beginningless priority by showing it is non-temporal and universally necessary.

Core Idea
God's priority over the world is not temporal; it is a necessary rational concept.

In this passage, Razi addresses two objections that question the coherence of God's precedence. The first objection concerns the nature of priority — is it temporal? The second challenges the very idea of a beginningless priority. Razi shows that the priority of God is not like time-priority, and that any worldview must admit something beginningless.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and identify the two objections
Read the Arabic and translation to see the two answers Razi gives. Notice how he handles each objection separately.
The objections are numbered second and third.
2
Understand the first answer about non-temporal priority
Razi says precedence of some temporal parts over others is not by time itself. Consider how this applies to God's priority over creation.
This is from the discussion on the origination of bodies.
3
Understand the second answer about universal necessity of beginninglessness
Razi argues that regardless of whether one believes the world is created or eternal, one must admit something beginningless. This shows the concept is inevitable.
Thus the objection fails.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجواب عن السؤال الثاني : أنا ذكرنا في أول مسألة حدوث الأجسام أن تقدم بعض أجزاء الزمان على البعض ليس بالزمان، فتقدم ذات الباري تعالى على العالم من هذا الجنس. والجواب عن السؤال الثالث: وهو السؤال الطاعن في قولنا : الباري تعالى سابق على العالم سبقا لا أول له - فاعلم أن هذا السؤال لازم على الكل سواء أقر ذلك الإنسان بحدوث العالم وقدم الصانع أو أنكر ذلك، وذلك لأنه إن أقر بحدوث العالم لزمه الإقرار بعدم لا أول له ، وإن قال بقدم العالم لزمه الإقرار بوجود لا أول له، فعلى جميع التقديرات لا بد من الإقرار بمعقول لا أول له، ولا بد من الإقرار بأمر له أول، وإذا كان الأمر كذلك زالت هذه الشبهات.
And the answer to the second question: We mentioned at the beginning of the question of the origination of bodies that the priority of some parts of time over others is not by time, so the priority of the essence of the Most High Creator over the world is of this kind. And the answer to the third question—which is the objection to our statement: 'The Most High Creator is prior to the world with a priority that has no beginning'—know that this question is binding on everyone, whether that person affirms the origination of the world and the eternity of the Maker or denies that. That is because if he affirms the origination of the world, he is compelled to affirm a non-existence that has no beginning; and if he says the world is eternal, he is compelled to affirm an existence that has no beginning. So in all cases, one must affirm an intelligible that has no beginning, and one must affirm something that has a beginning. When it is thus, these doubts are removed.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage is an objection-and-answer section. Razi responds to two objections: the second concerns the nature of time priority, and the third challenges the concept of a beginningless priority. For the second, he recalls that in the discussion of bodies' temporality, it was established that priority of some parts of time over others is not a temporal priority (bil-zaman), so God's priority over the world is of that non-temporal kind. For the third, he argues that the question about a beginningless priority is necessary for everyone: if one affirms the world's creation, he must affirm a beginningless non-existence; if one affirms the world's eternity, he must affirm a beginningless existence. Thus, in all cases, one must admit something beginningless, and this dispels the doubt.

Key Terms
سبق لا أول له
حدوث الأجسام
تقدم
زمان

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: God's priority over the world must be a temporal priority, meaning God existed before time and time is a container.
Correction: Razi explains that the priority of some temporal parts over others is not by time itself, so God's priority is non-temporal, an ontological precedence.

Checkpoint
According to Razi's answer to the third objection, what does one who affirms the world's creation necessarily admit?
A) A beginningless existence
B) A beginningless non-existence
C) That the world is eternal
D) That God has a beginning

Key Takeaway
God's beginningless priority is a rational necessity that does not rely on temporal categories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
You habitually think of God as existing 'before' the universe in a temporal sense. After this lesson, will you consciously reject that temporal image? What concrete step will you take to replace it with a non-temporal understanding of His priority?
?
Razi forces you to admit that any worldview must accept something beginningless. If you reject God's beginningless existence, what beginningless thing do you affirm in its place? How does that affect your accountability to a Creator?
?
This lesson shows that the objection to God's precedence is invalid because it is self-refuting. What objections do you still harbor in your heart against God's attributes? Will you submit to this rational proof today, or cling to your doubt? Promise a specific time tonight to reflect on this passage and pray for clarity.

Two Proofs for God's Permanence (Baqa')
Razi presents two arguments that God cannot cease to exist after having existed.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand two rational proofs demonstrating that God, once existing, cannot cease to exist.

Core Idea
God's existence is permanent; no cause can bring about His non-existence.

Imam Razi presents two rigorous philosophical arguments to defend the attribute of permanence (baqa') for God. These proofs show that once God exists, it is impossible for Him to cease to exist. The first proof eliminates all possible causes of non-existence, while the second proof demonstrates that if annihilation were possible, God would be contingent and thus originated—a contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the proofs carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation once to get the overall structure. Notice that Razi presents two distinct proofs, each with its own logical flow.
The first proof is a trilemma; the second is a conditional chain.
2
Analyze the first proof
Follow Razi's three possibilities for how non-existence could occur: by an annihilator, by an opposite, or by removal of a condition. See why each is impossible.
Focus on the reasoning for each branch—especially why annihilation by an agent is impossible and why eternal is stronger than originated.
3
Understand the second proof
Trace the implication: if non-existence were possible, essence would need a cause, which would make God originated—contradicting His necessity.
This proof relies on earlier premises about contingency and origination.
4
Reflect on the conclusion
Both proofs converge on the same conclusion: God's permanence is necessary. Consider why this attribute is essential in Islamic theology.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
واعلم أن المشايخ . رحمهم الله - احتجوا على بقاء الصانع بحجتين : . الحجة الأولى قالوا لو عدم بعد وجوده لكان إما أن يكون عدمه بإعدام معدم، أو بطريان ضد أو بانتفاء شرط، والأول محال لأن القدرة صفة مؤثرة، والعدم نفي محض، فيمتنع كون الإعدام بالفاعل ولا جائز أن يكون بطريان ضد؛ لأن هذا الضد محدث والقديم أقوى من المحدث، فكان اندفاع هذا الضد بسبب وجوده أولى من انعدامه بسبب طريان هذا المحدث، ولا جائز أن يكون بسبب زوال شرط لأن ذلك الشرط يجب أن يكون قديماً؛ لأن المحدث يمتنع أن يكون شرطا للقديم، وإذا كان كذلك كان الكلام في عدمه كالكلام في عدم القديم الأول، فيلزم التسلسل، وهو محال. الحجة الثانية : أنه لو صح عليه العدم لكانت ماهيته قابلة للعدم وللوجود، ولو كان كذلك لكان مفتقرًا إلى المؤثر، وكل مفتقر إلى المؤثر محدث، فيلزم أنه لو صح العدم عليه بعد وجود لكان محدثًا. وتقرير هذه المقدمات قد تقدم في مسألة حدوث الأجسام، ولما امتنع حدوثه امتنع عدمه بعد وجوده وبالله التوفيق.
And know that the masters—may God have mercy on them—argued for the permanence of the Maker with two proofs. The first proof: They said, if after His existence He were to cease to exist, then His non-existence would either be by the annihilation of an annihilator, or by the occurrence of an opposite, or by the removal of a condition. And the first is impossible because power is an effective attribute, and non-existence is pure negation, so it is impossible for annihilation to be from an agent. And it is not permissible that it be by the occurrence of an opposite, because this opposite is originated, and the eternal is stronger than the originated, so the repelling of this opposite due to His existence is more appropriate than His annihilation due to the occurrence of this originated. And it is not permissible that it be due to the removal of a condition, because that condition must be eternal; because the originated cannot be a condition for the eternal. And if it is so, then the discussion about its non-existence is like the discussion about the non-existence of the first eternal, leading to an infinite regress, which is impossible. The second proof: If non-existence were permissible for Him, then His essence would be receptive to non-existence and existence, and if so, He would be in need of an effective cause, and everything in need of an effective cause is originated, so it would entail that if non-existence were permissible for Him after existence, He would be originated. And the exposition of these premises has preceded in the question of the origination of bodies. And since His origination is impossible, His non-existence after His existence is impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 96

Commentary
This passage presents two proofs for God's eternal existence (بقاء) after having existed. The first proof: if God were to cease to exist, it would be either (a) by an annihilator's annihilation, (b) by the occurrence of an opposite, or (c) by the removal of a condition. (a) is impossible because power is an effective attribute and non-existence is pure negation, so annihilation by an agent is meaningless. (b) is impossible because the opposite is originated, and the eternal is stronger than the originated; its existence would repel the opposite rather than be annihilated by it. (c) is impossible because the condition would have to be eternal (since an originated condition cannot be a condition for the eternal), and then the same argument applies to that condition, leading to infinite regress. So all possibilities are impossible. The second proof: if annihilation were possible, then His essence would be receptive to both existence and non-existence, requiring an effective cause, and everything requiring an effective cause is originated, so He would be originated—a contradiction. Therefore, His permanence is necessary. The details of these premises were given earlier in the discussion of bodies' temporality.

Key Terms
بقاء
عدم
إعدام
ضد
شرط
ماهية
مؤثر
محدث

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: That God could be annihilated by the action of an agent (e.g., a powerful being).
Correction: Razi argues that annihilation is impossible because non-existence is pure negation, and power is an effective attribute that brings about existence, not non-existence.

Checkpoint
In the first proof, why does Razi reject the possibility that God's non-existence could be caused by the occurrence of an opposite?
A) Because opposites cannot affect the eternal
B) Because the opposite is originated and the eternal is stronger, so its existence would repel the opposite
C) Because conditions must be eternal
D) Because power is an effective attribute

Key Takeaway
God's permanence is rationally necessary because any scenario for His non-existence leads to absurdity (first proof) or contradiction (second proof).

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's existence is permanent and cannot cease, then your soul's reliance on Him must also be permanent. But have you ever lived a single day as if God might not be there tomorrow? What does that say about the reality of your faith?
?
The proof shows that no external cause can bring about God's non-existence. Yet we often fear that our circumstances or people can somehow diminish God's power in our lives. When have you acted as if a created thing could 'annihilate' God's support for you?
?
Razi teaches that God cannot be receptive to non-existence because that would make Him contingent. Are there areas of your life where you treat God as contingent—as if He needs your permission or effort to act? Reflect on a specific situation where you acted as though God's action depended on you.

The Proof That God's Essence Differs In Itself
Razi presents a proof by reductio ad absurdum that God's essence is essentially unique.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the central proof that God's essence must be different in itself from all other essences, based on the impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator.

Core Idea
God's essence cannot be equal to others without leading to absurdity.

Imam Razi now delivers his main proof for the essential difference of God. He argues that if God's essence were equal to others, then His unique attributes would require a cause, leading to an infinite regress or circular reasoning. This short but dense argument is foundational for Islamic theology.

Guided Path
1
Understand the context
Razi has previously defined that 'different by essence' means difference in the very reality of the essence, not by an additional attribute. This proof shows that equality is impossible.
The definition is crucial: difference is in the essence itself.
2
Read the proof carefully
Notice the conditional structure: 'If essence were equal... then attributes would be merely possible... then preponderance would require a cause...'
The argument is a reductio ad absurdum.
3
Identify the two impossible outcomes
If the cause is absent, we have preponderance without a preponderator, which is impossible. If the cause is present, then the cause's own particularization leads to circularity or infinite regress.
Both outcomes are logically impossible.
4
Conclude the proof
Since the assumption of equality leads to impossibility, the assumption must be false. Thus, God's essence is essentially unique.
This proof establishes tawhid in the essence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا عرفت هذا فنقول : قولنا : " الله تعالى مخالف لخلقه لذاته المخصوصة " المراد منه ما ذكرناه ولخصناه. وإذا لخصنا محل النزاع فنقول : الدليل على أنه تعالى مخالف لخلقه لذاته المخصوصة أنه لو كانت ذاته من حيث إنها تلك الذات مساوية لسائر الذوات - وقد عرفت أن الأشياء المتساوية في تمام الحقيقة يجب أن يصح على كل واحد منها ما صح على الآخر، وإذا كان كذلك كان اختصاص ذاته بصفته المخصوصة، وعدم اختصاصه بصفات المحدثات أمرًا جائزا ، فترجح ذلك الجائز على سائر الجائزات، إن لم يكن لأمر فقد ترجح الممكن لا عن مؤثر، وهو محال، وإن كان لأمر عاد الطلب في اختصاص ذاته بذلك الأمر، فيلزم إما الدور وإما التسلسل، وهما محالان، فثبت أن القول بكون ذاته سبحانه وتعالى مساوية لسائر الذوات في كونه ذاتا يفضي إلى أحد هذه المحالات فكان القول به محالا وبالله التوفيق.
And when you know this, we say: Our statement 'God (Exalted) is different from His creation by His specific essence' means what we have mentioned and summarized. And when we summarize the point of dispute, we say: The proof that He (Exalted) is different from His creation by His specific essence is that if His essence in so far as it is that essence were equal to other essences – and you have known that things equal in the entirety of reality must have whatever applies to one apply to the other – and if that is so, then His being particularized with His specific attribute and His not being particularized with the attributes of contingent things is a possibility (ja'iz). So if this possibility is preponderated over other possibilities, then if not for a cause, then a possible has been preponderated without a preponderator, which is impossible; and if it is for a cause, then the request returns regarding the particularization of His essence with that cause, necessitating either circularity (dawr) or infinite regress (tasalsul), both of which are impossible. Thus it is established that the statement that His essence (Glory be to Him and Exalted is He) is equal to other essences in being an essence leads to one of these impossibilities, so that statement is impossible. And with God is success.
Source pages p. 98

Commentary
This passage presents the main proof of the author's position. First, he clarifies that his phrase 'God is different by His specific essence' is to be understood as he has already explained – meaning essential difference not requiring an additional attribute. Then he states the proof: assume God's essence were equal to other essences in every respect. Things that are equal in complete reality must share all properties. If that were so, then God's having His specific attribute (like necessary existence) and not having the attributes of contingent things would be merely possible – it could be or not be. But in reality, He does have that specific attribute. This preponderance of one possible over others requires a cause (preponderator). If there is no cause, that is preponderance without a preponderator, which is impossible. If there is a cause, then that cause's own particularization to God would need another cause, leading to circularity or infinite regress. Since all these outcomes are impossible, the initial assumption that God's essence is equal to other essences must be false. Thus, God's essence differs in itself.

Key Terms
الدليل (proof)
المساواة (equality)
الجائز (possible)
الترجيح (preponderance)
المؤثر (preponderator)
الدور (circularity)
التسلسل (infinite regress)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think that God's essence could be equal in 'being an essence' but different by additional attributes.
Correction: Razi shows that if essence is equal, then even the specific attribute would be merely possible, requiring a cause, leading to infinite regress or preponderance without cause.

Checkpoint
What does the proof conclude about the statement that God's essence is equal to other essences?
A) It is necessary.
B) It is possible.
C) It is impossible because it leads to preponderance without a preponderator or circularity/regress.
D) It is true but only with additional attributes.

Key Takeaway
The impossibility of preponderance without a preponderator proves that God's essence cannot be equal to any other essence.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
If God's essence were not unique, what basis would you have to be certain that your worship is directed to the true God, and not to a being that merely shares accidental similarities? How does the impossibility of equal essence steady your heart in tawhid?
?
The proof shows that assuming equality leads to an infinite regress or circularity. Are there areas in your life where you assume your own standard is equal to God's, leading to a similar logical (and spiritual) dead end? What would it mean to accept that God's essence is utterly unique and therefore His commands are not to be weighed against your own?
?
The preponderator must be something outside the possible. Reflect: Do you ever try to be the preponderator in your own life, assigning weight to your actions independent of God's decree? How does this proof call you to acknowledge that only God can truly preponderate existence?

Three Positions on God's Existence and Essence
Al-Razi enumerates three positions on identity of existence and essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three classical positions on whether God's existence is identical to His essence, as enumerated by Fakhr al-Din al-Razi.

Core Idea
Three positions, one question: is God's existence the same as His essence?

This passage from al-Razi's Al-Arbaeen presents the three possible positions on the relationship between God's existence and His essence. The debate is fundamental to Islamic theology and philosophy, with each position carrying implications for how we understand divine attributes. Al-Razi succinctly lays out the views of the Ash'ari school, Ibn Sina, and his own preferred view, clearly delineating the conceptual differences.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage and understand the question
Read the Arabic passage once, then the translation. Notice that al-Razi asks whether God's existence is identical to His essence and then states there are only three possible positions.
The question is phrased as a problem (مسألة).
2
Identify the first position (Ash'ari view)
The first position holds that the term 'existent' applies to God and contingent things with two different concepts. This is attributed to al-Ash'ari and al-Basri.
This is a form of equivocity (اشتراك لفظي).
3
Identify the second position (Ibn Sina's view)
The second position holds that 'existent' is a single concept, but for God it is bare existence not accidental to any essence, distinguished only by a negative qualification. This is Ibn Sina's view.
This is a form of univocity with a distinction.
4
Identify the third position (al-Razi's chosen view)
The third position holds that 'existent' is a single concept and it is an attribute accidental to God's essence. This is the position al-Razi favors.
This is the view of 'a great group' and the principles.
5
Note the cross-reference to a previous discussion
Al-Razi notes that the first position was already discussed in the question of whether non-existence is a thing, so he does not repeat it here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المسألة السادسة
في أن وجود الله تعالى هل هو نفس حقيقته أم لا ؟
المذاهب الممكنة في هذه المسألة لا تزيد على ثلاثة :
أحدها قول من يقول : إطلاق لفظ الموجود على واجب الوجود وعلى ممكن الوجود ليس بحسب معنى واحد بل بحسب مفهومين وهذا هو قول أبي الحسن الأشعري وأبي الحسين البصري، وأتباعهما.
والقول الثاني : هو أن وقوع لفظ الموجود على الواجب وعلى الممكن بحسب مفهوم واحد، إلا أن ذلك المفهوم غير مقارن لشيء من الماهيات، بل هو وجود مجرد، وإنما يتميز عن سائر الوجودات بقيد سلبي، وهو أنه غير عارض لشيء من الماهيات، ووجودات الممكنات أوصاف عارضة لماهيات الممكنات وهذا القول
هو اختيار أبي علي بن سينا في جميع كتبه.
والقول الثالث : وهو أن وقوع لفظ الموجود على الواجب وعلى الممكن بحسب مفهوم واحد، وذلك المفهوم صفة عارضة لماهية الحق سبحانه وتعالى وتقدس، ولحقيقته المخصوصة وهو المختار عندنا طائفة عظيمة وعند الأصول.
فأما القول الأول فقد تكلمنا فيه في مسألة أن المعدوم شيء أم لا، فلا نعيد.
The sixth question: Whether the existence of God, exalted is He, is identical to His essence or not? The possible positions on this question do not exceed three: One of them is the saying of those who say: The application of the term 'existent' to the Necessary Existence and to the possible existence is not according to a single meaning but rather according to two concepts—this is the saying of Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri and their followers. The second position: that the occurrence of the term 'existent' upon the Necessary and upon the possible is according to a single concept, except that that concept is not concomitant with any of the essences, rather it is bare existence, and it is distinguished from other existences only by a negative qualification, namely that it is not accidental to any of the essences, while the existences of possibles are attributes accidental to the essences of possibles—this position is the choice of Abu Ali ibn Sina in all his books. The third position: that the occurrence of the term 'existent' upon the Necessary and upon the possible is according to a single concept, and that concept is an attribute accidental to the essence of the Truth, glory be to Him and exalted, and to His specific reality—and this is the chosen position according to us, a great group, and according to the principles. As for the first position, we have already discussed it in the question of whether non-existence is a thing or not, so we do not repeat it.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration and classification of the three possible positions concerning whether God's existence is identical to His essence. Al-Razi begins by stating the question: is God's existence the same as His essence or not? He then states that there are only three possible positions. The first position, attributed to Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Abu al-Husayn al-Basri, holds that the term 'existent' is applied to God and to contingent things with two different concepts, i.e., univocally. The second position, attributed to Ibn Sina, holds that 'existent' is applied with a single concept, but that concept is not accidental to any essence; rather it is bare existence, distinguished only by a negative qualification (that it does not inhere in any essence), while contingent existences are accidents inhering in essences. The third position, which al-Razi indicates is the chosen one among his group and many scholars, holds that the concept of existence is a single concept but it is an attribute accidental to the specific essence of God. Al-Razi then notes that the first position has already been treated in a previous discussion (on whether non-existence is a thing), so he will not repeat it here. The passage sets up the debate by clearly delineating the three views, with the second view to be refuted in what follows.

Key Terms
وجود
ماهية
واجب الوجود
ممكن الوجود
اشتراك معنوي
قيد سلبي
عارض
مجرد

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some might think there are more than three possible positions on this question.
Correction: Al-Razi explicitly states that the possible positions do not exceed three (لا تزيد على ثلاثة), making this a complete and exhaustive classification.

Checkpoint
According to al-Razi's enumeration, which position holds that the term 'existent' is applied to God and to contingent things with a single concept that is not accidental to any essence but is bare existence distinguished by a negative qualification?
A) The first position (al-Ash'ari and al-Basri)
B) The second position (Ibn Sina)
C) The third position (the chosen one)
D) None of the above

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi presents three exhaustive positions on whether God's existence is identical to His essence, with the third being the one he favors.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Which of the three positions do you find most intuitive when you consider your own belief in God? What does that preference reveal about how you imagine God's existence? Are you willing to examine that assumption critically in light of this scholarly debate?
?
The passage divides scholars into three camps on a fundamental question about God. How does knowing that there are such deep disagreements among great minds affect your humility when you recite 'Allahu Akbar'? Do you truly acknowledge that your understanding is limited?
?
If the third position is correct—that God's existence is an attribute accidental to His essence—then God's essence is even more fundamental than His existence. Does that thought make you feel distant from God, or does it deepen your awe? How can you cultivate a sense of awe for a God whose essence is beyond even existence?

Allah's Existence
beginner
4 min
Setting Up the Three Possibilities
Al-Razi outlines three possibilities for existence's relation to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the three logical possibilities regarding existence's relation to essence as a foundation for refuting Ibn Sina's view.

Core Idea
Existence is a single concept with three possible relations to essence: accidental, non-accidental, or neutral.

Al-Razi sets the stage by establishing that existence is a single concept, a point of agreement with Ibn Sina. He then presents the three possible ways existence can relate to essences. This tripartite classification is crucial for the subsequent refutation.

Guided Path
1
Read the opening claim
Read the first part where Al-Razi states that existence is a single concept and that Ibn Sina agrees. This is the common ground.
2
Identify the three possibilities
Find the three alternatives: existence necessitates being an accident, necessitates not being an accident, or is neutral. Notice the precise wording.
The third option is ‘does not necessitate either, both are possible’.
3
Reflect on the classification
Ask yourself why these three are exhaustive and mutually exclusive. This will become the framework for the proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما القول الثاني الذي اختاره أبو علي بن سينا فنقول إنه باطل، ويدل عليه
الأول : أن الوجود من حيث إنه وجود مفهوم واحد على ما دلت عليه الدلائل، ووافقنا فيه أبو علي بن سينا.
وأيضًا هذه المسألة متفرعة على هذا القول، فنقول : الوجود من حيث إنه وجود إما أن يقتضي أن يكون عارضًا لماهية أو يقتضي أن لا يكون عارضًا لماهية
أو لا يقتضي لا أن يكون عارضًا ولا أن يكون غير عارض، بل الأمران جائزان عليه، فإن اقتضى الوجود من حيث إنه وجود أن يكون عارضًا لماهية من الماهيات وجب أن يكون وجود واجب الوجود عارضًا لماهية من الماهيات؛ فقوله : إنه وجود مجرد غير عارض لشيء من الماهيات قول باطل وما إن اقتضى الوجود أن يكون غير عارض لشيء من الماهيات وجب أن لا يكون شيء من الوجودات عارضًا لشيء من الماهيات ،البتة فهذه الممكنات إما أن لا تكون موجودة أصلا وإن كانت موجودة كانت وجوداتها نفس ماهياتها، فيكون لفظ الوجود واقعا على الموجودات بالاشتراك اللفظي لا بالاشتراك المعنوي، وقد بينا أن ذلك باطل وأن هذا البحث متفرع على أن لفظ الموجود واقع على الواجب والممكن بالاشتراك المعنوي.
وأما إن قلنا الوجود من حيث إنه وجود لا يقتضي أن يكون عارضًا لماهية ولا أن يكون غير عارض لها، فحينئذ يمتنع أن يصير عارضًا أو غير عارض إلا لسبب منفصل، فوجود واجب الوجود لا يصير مجردًا إلا بسبب منفصل، فوجود واجب الوجود لا يصير مجردًا إلا بسبب منفصل فيكون واجب الوجود لذاته واجب الوجود لغيره، وهو محال.
صبح
وأيضا : قد عرفت أن الماهيات المتساوية في تمام تلك الماهية كل ما على كل واحد منها صح على كلها، فإذن كل ما صح على جميع الموجودات العارضة لماهيات الممكنات وجب أن يصح على واجب الوجود، وكل ما ثبت لواجب الوجود وجب أن يثبت لوجودات جميع الماهيات الممكنات، وكل ذلك باطل قطعاً، ولما ثبت بهذا البرهان القطعي امتناع هذه الأقسام، ثبت أن القول الذي اختاره أبو علي بن سينا قول مردود.
As for the second position which Abu Ali ibn Sina chose, we say that it is false, and the following indicates that: First: that existence, insofar as it is existence, is a single concept as indicated by the proofs, and Abu Ali ibn Sina agreed with us on that. Also, this question is derived from this position, so we say: Existence, insofar as it is existence, either necessitates that it is an accident of an essence, or necessitates that it is not an accident of an essence, or does not necessitate either that it is an accident or that it is not an accident, rather both are possible for it. If existence insofar as it is existence necessitates that it is an accident of an essence, then the existence of the Necessary Existence must be an accident of an essence; so his statement that it is bare existence not accidental to any essence is a false statement. And if existence necessitates that it is not an accident of any essence, then it must be that no existence is accidental to any essence at all; so these possibles either are not existent at all, or if they are existent, their existences are identical to their essences, then the term existence applies to existents by verbal homonymy (ishtirak lafzi) not by conceptual commonality (ishtirak ma'nawi); and we have already shown that this is false and that this investigation is derived from the fact that the term existent applies to the Necessary and the possible by conceptual commonality. And if we say that existence insofar as it is existence does not necessitate that it is an accident of an essence nor that it is not an accident of it, then it becomes impossible for it to become an accident or not an accident except due to a separate cause; so the existence of the Necessary Existence does not become bare except due to a separate cause, thus the Necessary Existence would be necessary by itself necessary by another, which is impossible. Also: you have known that the essences equal in the entirety of that essence — everything that applies to each one of them applies to all of them; therefore, everything that applies to all existences accidental to the essences of possibles must apply to the Necessary Existence, and everything established for the Necessary Existence must be established for the existences of all possible essences; and all that is absolutely false. And when it is established by this decisive proof the impossibility of these divisions, it is established that the position chosen by Abu Ali ibn Sina is a rejected position.
Source pages p. 101

Commentary
This passage presents a proof against Ibn Sina's view that God's existence is bare existence not accidental to any essence. Al-Razi first notes that existence as such is a single concept, a point on which Ibn Sina agrees. Then he considers three possibilities regarding existence's relation to essence: (1) existence necessitates being an accident of an essence, (2) existence necessitates not being an accident, or (3) it is neutral. If (1), then God's existence would be accidental, contradicting Ibn Sina's claim. If (2), then no existence is accidental, so contingent existences would either be non-existent or identical to their essences, implying that 'existence' is applied only verbally, not by conceptual commonality—which was already refuted. If (3), then whether existence is accidental or not depends on an external cause, so God's existence would become bare only by an external cause, making God's necessity dependent on another, which is impossible. Then a supplementary argument: if all accidental existences of possibles share a property, that property must apply to God; conversely, what holds for God holds for all such existences—leading to absurdity. Thus all possible interpretations are refuted, and Ibn Sina's position is false.

Key Terms
اقتضاء
عارض
ماهية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the first foundational point Al-Razi makes about existence?
A) Existence is a single concept
B) Existence is always an accident
C) Existence is never an accident
D) Existence is neutral

Key Takeaway
The three possibilities for existence's relation to essence—accident, non-accident, or neutral—form the logical basis for refuting Ibn Sina's view.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi treats existence as a single concept that demands logical analysis. Do you live as if the existence of Allah is a single, undeniable reality, or do you allow fragmented doubts to cloud your certainty? What concrete step will you take today to strengthen your conviction in His existence?
?
This passage shows that existence can be accidental or necessary. When you reflect on your own existence, do you sense it as a mere accident or as something grounded in a Necessary Being? How does your answer shape your daily gratitude and dependence on Allah?

Refuting the First Two Possibilities
Al-Razi refutes the first two possibilities about existence's relation to essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi refutes the first two possibilities and why each leads to an absurdity.

Core Idea
If existence must be an accident, God's existence becomes accidental; if it must not, contingent existence becomes identical to essence.

Having set up the three possibilities, al-Razi now tackles the first two. He shows that assuming existence necessarily is an accident makes God's existence accidental, contradicting Ibn Sina's claim. Assuming it necessarily is not an accident leads to the absurd consequence that contingent things either do not exist or are identical to their essences, which undermines the common meaning of existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the first refutation
Read how Al-Razi handles the first possibility (existence necessitates being an accident). Notice the direct implication for God's existence.
2
Read the second refutation
Read how the second possibility (necessitates not being an accident) leads to either non-existence of contingents or identity of existence and essence.
Pay attention to the conclusion about verbal homonymy.
3
Connect to the broader proof
Understand that these refutations eliminate two of the three possibilities, leaving only the third for further analysis.

Key Takeaway
Both the first and second possibilities are refuted: the first makes God accidental, the second destroys the common meaning of existence.

?

How does the reality that your existence is a gift added to your essence serve as a daily reminder of your absolute dependence on Allah? Will you let that awareness change how you live this day?
?

Are you willing to learn the precise language needed to speak truthfully about Allah, even if it is difficult? Refuting the Third Possibility and Final Proof
Al-Razi refutes the third possibility and gives a supplementary argument to seal the proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Razi refutes the third possibility and closes with a supplementary argument that completes the proof.

Core Idea
The neutral option makes God's necessity depend on another, and the shared-properties argument eliminates all remaining ambiguity.

The third possibility—that existence is neutral regarding accidence—leads to the absurdity that God's bare existence would require an external cause, making God necessary by another. Al-Razi then presents a supplementary argument based on shared properties across essences, reinforcing the impossibility of Ibn Sina's position.

Guided Path
1
Read the refutation of neutrality
Read how Al-Razi handles the third possibility: if existence is neutral, then whether it is accidental depends on an external cause, so God's existence would be bare only by an external cause, making God necessary by another.
2
Read the supplementary argument
Read the argument about equal essences: if a property applies to all accidental existences of possibles, it must apply to God; and vice versa, leading to absurdity.
Notice that this argument does not depend on the three possibilities.
3
Conclude the proof
With all three possibilities refuted, Al-Razi concludes that Ibn Sina's position is false.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?
If you truly believe that nothing can be shared between Allah and His creation, what must you change about how you view your own existence? Are you living as though your existence is dependent on Him every moment?
?
The supplementary argument shows that any property of contingents must also apply to Allah if essences are equal—an absurdity. In your daily life, do you ever fall into the trap of comparing Allah to His creation? How can you actively combat this tendency?
